\\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. \\\"Allowed\\\" : \\\"Denied\\\");\\n263:         bldr.append(\\\" operation = \\\").append(action.operation());\\n264:         bldr.append(\\\" from host = \\\").append(context.clientAddress().getHostAddress());\\n265:         bldr.append(\\\" on resource = \\\");\\n266:         appendResourcePattern(action.resourcePattern(), bldr);\\n267:         bldr.append(\\\" for request = \\\").append(ApiKeys.forId(context.requestType()).name);\\n268:         bldr.append(\\\" with resourceRefCount = \\\").append(action.resourceReferenceCount());\\n269:         bldr.append(\\\" based on rule \\\").append(rule);\\n270:         return bldr.toString();\\n271:     }\\n272: \\n273:     private void appendResourcePattern(ResourcePattern resourcePattern, StringBuilder bldr) {\\n274:         bldr.append(SecurityUtils.resourceTypeName(resourcePattern.resourceType()))\\n275:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n276:             .append(resourcePattern.patternType())\\n277:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n278:             .append(resourcePattern.name());\\n279:     }\\n280: \\n281:     private void logAuditMessage(\\n282:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\\n283:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n284:         Action action,\\n285:         MatchingRule rule\\n286:     ) {\\n287:         switch (rule.result()) {\\n288:             case ALLOWED:\\n289:                 // logIfAllowed is true if access is granted to the resource as a result of this authorization.\\n290:                 // In this case, log at debug level. If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n308:                 }\\n309:         }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\\n323:         // the first divergence point.\\n324:         //\\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1. // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\\n377:             i++;\\n378:         }\\n379:         return i;\\n380:     }\\n381: \\n382:     private void checkSection(\\n383: \\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306: }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which exemplar.resourceName().substring(0, matchesUpTo),\\n415:                     exemplar.patternType(),\\n416:                     exemplar.principal(),\\n417: Authorizer implementation starts loading its metadata.</li>\n51:  *   <li>Broker starts SocketServer to accept connections and process requests.</li>\n52:  *   <li>For each listener, SocketServer waits for authorization metadata to be available in the\n53:  *       authorizer before accepting connections. The future returned by {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}\n54:  *       for each listener must return only when authorizer is ready to authorize requests on the listener.</li>\n55:  *   <li>Broker accepts connections. The following tags are automatically added to all metrics registered:\n64:  * <code>config</code> set to <code>authorizer.class.name</code>, <code>class</code> set to the Authorizer class name,\n65:  * and <code>role</code> set to either <code>broker</code> or <code>controller</code>.\n66:  * <p>\n67:  * <b>Threading model:</b>\n68:  * <ul>\n69:  *   <li>All authorizer operations including authorization and ACL updates must be thread-safe.</li>\n70:  *   <li>ACL update methods are asynchronous. If ACL updates require remote communication which may block,\n74:  *       return a future that is completed asynchronously when the remote operation completes. This enables\n75:  *       the caller to process other requests on the request threads without blocking.</li>\n76:  *   <li>Any threads or thread pools used for processing remote operations asynchronously can be started during\n77:  *       {@link #start(AuthorizerServerInfo)}.
